RATING: 9
A coop game where all players must cooperate to successfully win the game. Of course, evading and shooting zombies are a great part of the game, but achieving the objectives is paramount. Game is not too long, rules are not too complex and the danger of being overrun by zombies is always a factor...

-1 For 2 Annoying rules: The 'Firing rule' and the 'No more zombies, every zombies of that type move again (reason for more than half of my Survivors death). Nothing a few houserules can't change, still...
-1 For Road/Building Tiles that curves, making them more difficult to align and keep them together than it should be... 
+1 For the general high quality of every pieces of the game (Colored minis, cards, tokens, etc...)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
I played this game just once, so these are mostly impressions that may change after multiple plays.

This is the biggest mass of stupid rules I've ever seen and it rappresents everything that is wrong with Kickstarter: all miniatures and no testing. Zombicide is really just the cooperative version of "Zombies!!!" with some cooler miniatures and higher pretensions. 

Here's my list of everything that's wrong with Zombicide:
- Zombies' Mitosis: I'd like to start from a common criticism. This rule is just stupid. It looks like the designers were drunk while trying to figure out how to randomly determine where a zombi should go, when they could go to two different places, and one of them said: "Wait a second! How about mitosis?". And all the others answered: "Coooooool!". Couldn't they just find a random system to determine where the zombi should go? Is this just to increase the number of zombies? In this case, couldn't they find a decent other way to increase them? Like cards or whatever??
- The Order of Targets: This rule isn't just stupid but it's also damaging to the gameplay. I don't even want to talk about the fact that I cannot target a room where there's a survivor without killing him. The biggest problem is that I cannot decide which zombi I kill, so I can't make tactical decisiona. This problem gets even worse with berseker zombies, which make the game really ridiculous.
- There's a Storehouse in my Bathtub: I'm really shocked by the fact that people can search in a room without end. This is not just a problem for the internal logic of the game. I understand that games can't always be logical. The problem is that this rule makes every game insanely repetitive: You start the game, find a room and begin to collect items while still few zombies come out every turn. There's no reason not to do this. So every time you play you spend the first turns drawing items from a pile of cards until you're ready to actually start the game.
- The First Player Enigma: This is a smaller issue but I don't like that players have to decide who goes first every turn. It's the perfect way to make the game longer for no reason. I understand that this depends a lot on the people you're playing with, but still I dislike the fact that I can spend 10 minutes arguing just to decide who should go first.

I know a lot of people like this game, but this is not just a matter of taste: this game is poorly designed. There's so much that could have been improved.

This (game) will probably bring an end to my interest in zombie games.

Is there anything else? no... really.

RATING: N/A
Zombicide is a collaborative game in which players take the role of a survivor – each with unique abilities – and harness both their skills and the power of teamwork against the hordes of unthinking undead! Zombies are predictable, stupid but deadly, controlled by simple rules and a deck of cards. Unfortunately for you, there are a LOT more zombies than you have bullets.

Find weapons, kill zombies. The more zombies you kill, the more skilled you get; the more skilled you get, the more zombies appear. The only way out is zombicide!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In the interest of full disclosure, I was one of the many who backed this game while it was on Kickstarter, so go ahead and assume whatever you want about my biases based on that.  I bought a fat stack of minis, and got a decent game as a bonus.

As the name implies, there's very little horror and a lot of zombie-shooting, zombie-smashing, and zombie-chainsawing.  As a Left 4 Dead player, I approve.  The rulebook isn't great, and there are some minor rules ambiguities, and some rules I just don't care for, but it's FUN, dammit.  Too many tiny plastic zombies for it to not be.

EDIT: Really wish they had rules for playing with 7 or more players for us Kickstarter folks.  I've got 9 heroes, with more on the way, but the game gets too easy if I play with more than 6?

EDIT: OK, the first rating (8) was good for the first scenario, but after playing a few of the others, going to have to downgrade this a bit.  Scenario 1 has you scavenging around a town for necessary foodstuffs to help the group last in the post-apocalyptic world.  It's hard, and tense, but in the way that all good co-ops are hard. It's also a very long scenario.

After trying several other scenarios, it almost feels like Scenario 1 was the one that the game was built for, and the rest are all afterthoughts.  Afterthoughts that have neither the challenge nor the fun factor of the game we thought we were playing.  I'll try the rest of them, since I've seen the game's potential. I'm keeping an eye out for fan-built scenarios, and might build some of my own, but some of these scenarios that come with the game are just poorly designed.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
It's so close to being a perfect zombie game. The mini's are gorgeous (and plentiful), the tiles look naturalistic (and are huge), and there's a good variety of zombies. Even a majority of the rules work very intuitively - how zombies move, how people move, what people can do, etc. There are two big flaws about it though - while the majority of the rules work well, there are a handful that work but come across as non-intuitive or un-thematic (targeting priority and driving cars, namely). The second flaw is that the rulebook scenario's are not very well balanced or diverse.

Ultimately, what I love most about this game is the sandbox nature. Even though the the rulebook scenarios are all rather similar, just the tiles and stuff you get is enough to play great games for a long time, especially with houserules.

RATING: 3
This game suffers from the leadership syndrome where, even if you play with 4 people, it feels like the only one to play is the most knowledgable player.

The different characters are well designed and make heavy allusions, but it's mostly cosmetic.

The game starts hard, where luck is an important aspect; and once you are well equipped, the game feels easier...

It can also feel repetitive unfortunately... But you have a lot of scenarios which try to renew each game. I still find it repetitive... Just like in (MMO)RPG video games where you have thousand of different quests with different stories but they are basically all about going to A and collect B.

Avoid this game at all cost if you don't want to suffer from the leadership syndrome.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.99
Dynamic game play with multiple variable missions for fun zombie co-op fun.

Game is challenging as players start off defenseless and level together to battle hords of zombies. Variety of characters, expansions, missions, maps and objectives really helps round out the experience and make the game feel fresh.

Humor is spot on and timely.

Pro:
Great components
lots of unique characters (and celebrity add on packs)
Miniatures! are nicely made and art is colourful and engaging
variation of play! With missions and character abilities and random spawns different objectives the game has lots of replay ability
Noise making mechanic adds dynamic to the game (not something I've seen in other mission based co-op games)

Con:
Longer set up time
Cost (she is a bit pricey but I think well worth it)
Table Captain syndrome exists as more experienced players can run the board

Miss-able turns: There are times in the game when a player (or multiple players) have to idle their turn. Either the situation/objective or other character abilities mean that players are unable to really move or go anywhere without actually hurting the team. I've played games where I had to skip my turn for 4 rounds in a row because we would make too much noise. So keep that in mind

All in all, I would still love to own this game and some expansions. I would caution folks to look into each season as everyone will have their favorite and I don't think all character packs are necessary (although they are neat!)

RATING: 7
Volt szerencsém a kipróbáláskor egy szinte teljes Zombicide kollekciót megnézni, nagyon impozáns látvány! Aki figurafestésre adja a fejét, annak nem ezzel a gyűjteménnyel kell kezdenie:) Nagyon ráfeküdtek a szerzők, amennyit láttam belőle, az alapján tényleg kihozzák a témából a maximumot. Még könyveket is kiadtak hozzá... Aki erre rácuppan, a végtelenségig játszhat vele: sok tucatnyi pályaelem, több száz figura, kártya lett hozzá kiadva, térfogatra kb. 8-10 alapjátéknak felel meg a teljes gyűjtemény (és még nincs vége szerintem). Tényleg egy külön kis univerzum.

És hogy a partinkról is essen szó: Ebben a műfajban talán ez a játék tetszett eddig a legjobban! A szabályrendszer a kategóriához képest nagyon egyszerű. Nem tököltek mindenféle sebzés-tokenekkel, a játékosoknak csak 2 élete van, a zombik pedig egyenesen fogyóeszközök:) Tucatjával lehet ölni őket (a sláger a kocsival való gázolás volt) és tucatjával is teremnek újra minden sarkon vagy a csatornában. Ennek megfelelően a győzelem vagy vereség nem nüanszokon múlik, hanem ha nem bírunk velük, előbb-utóbb ellepnek minket a zombik... Nem azt mondom, hogy a kedvencem lesz, de ha ilyen típussal kellene játszanom, ezt választanám, mert pl. a pálya összeállítása nagyságrendekkel egyszerűbb, mint egy Odalentben vagy főleg Earth Rebornban, és vannak egész rövid pályák is, ha arra van igény. Ha több dobozt is megpiszkálunk a nagy gyűjteményből, akkor azért elég horror lehet az elpakolásnál szétválogatni hogy mi hova tartozik... 
A játékban a nehézségi szintet elég lazán oldották meg: egyfelől minden pályának van egy "hivatalos" nehézsége, másfelől ha több szereplőt viszünk, akkor könnyebb a játék. Tehát lehet akár mindenki két emberrel és akkor dupla annyi akciónk van. Így elég könnyű belőni magunknak a testhezálló nehézségi szintet.
Aki szereti ezeket a mászkálós-lövöldözőseket, az mindenképp próbálja ki!

RATING: 6

Both have a reliance on many decks of cards to generate the body of the story. The game art was thematic and the minis were a great addition to the theme. However, the game felt more tactical, almost like the heroes were an elite commando team rather than a scattered group of survivors, and there wasn't much of a sense of overall urgency or dread. Overall, this seemed like a more mid-complexity dungeon crawl rather than a zombie apocalypse survival horror.

RATING: N/A
I enjoyed this game, but it's not exactly what I was hoping for. A co-op game that has individual defeat feels a little harsh to me. What I mean is someone may get caught in a flood of zombies with their last character and they're out until the game is over, which can be a very long time if it's the right scenario.

The rule book is confusing, they have the pictures which help some but in most cases if they covered something in a picture they don't bother to talk about it in the text, which can lead to a frustrating 'where's waldo' feel trying to figure the rules out.

One play through is all it took for most of those I play with to decide they didn't want to play this game anymore.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
FINAL THOUGHTS: I'm lowering my score for this game. Not because I like it less, but because I now have a lot more experience with board games. Technically, I have a lot of issues with this game. The character cards are awful. The variable power concept is poorly designed and probably as a money making ploy. I still enjoy Zombicide, but honestly it feels more like a good tool kit than a well designed game. The setup is terrible. It's hard to remember all of the rules. And I feel like I can only bring this out with people who truly enjoy a long and slightly more complex game.

This game is the reigning champion for my gamer group.  It is always the expected main course to a night of trying lots of different games.  Everything is just leading up to a cooperative romp around the streets of Zombicide.  And I can't blame them.  It is strategic and well balanced.  It has the potential to be easy or very hard.  The scenarios range in super short to kinda long but not too long.  There is purpose and everyone can feel like a useful component to the team.  It is just as much fun with 2 people as it is with 6.  It is all around a great game.

Update 7/8/2013: I'm upping my original score from an 8 to a 9.  Now that I really grasp the rules, this game is tons of fun.  I played a scenario for the second time and I can see how even with only the challenges in the physical manual, this game can be fresh every time.  I want the expansions because I love this game, but honestly I don't think they are needed to have several more years of fun.

Update 4/27/2013: I got to play the first scenario in the manual with 3 friends tonight. We used all of the zombie spawn cards for the full experience. As we got further up in levels we took a few risks and ended up loosing two people, but we managed to win in the end. There are still a few rules I am unclear about. I think overall it was about 95% correct. I'll have to re-read the updated rules and the FAQ a few more times. It was a close game. We were on edge as we started to see more and more zombies enter the map. We feared the runners. There were times that we thought we would lose and there were times that we managed some hilarious zombie slaughtering good fun.  Overall, this game is a hit. Now I want the expansions.

Finally tried the tutorial scenario tonight.  It was actually pretty fun all alone.  The tutorial is meant to be extremely easy but I ended up losing two of my people before reaching the objective.  I made a mistake following the rules and forgot to spawn in zombies when I first walked into a room and didn't realize it until I was almost done moving all of my survivors.  And on top of that one of my searches produced an extra zombie in the room.  So, basically the room two of my people were sitting in had three zombies all of a sudden and there was nothing I could really do about it.  So, I let Ned die, even though he had his free search and a flashlight.  I figured I could still win for sure since Josh was the other survivor in the room and he has the slippery skill.  I lost Amy in that room too on my next turn, but Josh had enough action points to walk into the room with the objective and pick it up.  Josh didn't get attacked because I had Phil shooting from outside to make noise.  Technically I only lost two, but I kept playing for fun to see if Phil could get Josh out of the building.  He did but it cost him his life.  Overall, I can see the immense amount of strategy involved.  If I had that much fun by myself, I can imagine that playing with a bunch of friends would be a blast.

RATING: 7
I'm not sure if this is an interesting take on cooperative gaming, or bad mechanics. Zombicide's targeting hierarchy is sure to leave some shaking their heads. It definitely forces you to think outside the box as you and your teammates attempt to tackle objectives. Often, grouping survivors together can be disastrous. Which wouldn't be such a bad thing if it weren't so unnatural. Where Zombicide excels is in it's simple rules set and quick gameplay. There's really not much to it, which means you can jump right in and start blasting and hacking away. Spawning mechanics assure plenty of zombies to keep everyone busy. And need I mention the minis are fantastic? Overall, is a great looking game that provides some light, frenzied fun. Happy to have it.

RATING: 7.25
Great game if only for the company that created it. In my opinion, I think they realized that game nerds are going hack your game no matter what you do/build and so they actually just built it into their game/philosophy.

Their website has a program you can download to create your own tiles to use in scenarios you create. In conjunction, they encourage you to create your characters to use beyond those provided. Also, they've just released an ipad app (!) to use in concert with their standard set-up. Finally, all of this DIY material is further encouraged by the community that they've encouraged where you can submit your own tile designs, scenarios, etc.

All in - Very fun game. I'm personally a little hazy on how the sound mechanism works in-game but a solid game nonetheless. A bit too unwieldy for non-gamers, at least on the first go of it. I'd personally like a campaign-style component wherein equipment/injuries/advancements/etc. are carried from game to game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Rating for Zombicide plus all expansions.

Yes, Zombicide as a whole system has its obvious flaws. Yes, some gameplay elements are thematically unsound. No, this does not affect the game in any bad way unless you houserule them (these gameplay elements balance the game; you should not try to change these or you will break the game). Yes, this is ameritrash in its absolute 99.8% purest form. Yes, it's very luck based. Yes, there is indeed only very little strategic value.

Despite all this; play Zombicide on any day with any group of any number of people - new and veteran hobbyists alike - and you WILL have fun.

It doesn't matter if some gameplay elements are flawed. It doesn't matter that some characters are more valuable than others. It doesn't matter if not much happens for a few turns. Nothing matters, because you WILL have a blast. The whole evening. Shooting and killing zombies. Digging through trash to find an awesome weapon. Shouting at other players to decide who should or can do the most damage to the most threatening group of zombies. Trying to run away from an abomination up until someone finally finds that motherf*****g gas canister.

Any day playing Zombicide is filled with fun, laughter and sometimes heroic stories which can stick in your brain for weeks on end.

The only real downside is that there is player elimination involved. Which is always bad in any game that can take a few hours to complete.

RATING: 2
The problem with Zombicide is the rules. They managed to take an interesting theme, make good components for it and then screw the gameplay.
Mowing down Zombies is fun, but without them being a threat for the most part and the tactics resulting in "well, if we don't have bad card draws, we'll just run threw the scenario" with no interesting decisions to make, just moving from tile to tile, searching till you get the right cards, rolling dice again and again with no planning required...

The gameplay of Zombicide is dull. They stole from Last Night On Earth so much and made an overall worse game by a mile.

CMON is good at marketing!

RATING: 7.5
Fun, fast zombie shooter. There is very little to the game apart from running around and killing zombies, but the game play is so fast and smooth, the rules are so easy to teach, and the game is so fun to play that it does perfectly what a light game like this should do: entertain thoroughly without bogging game play down with excessive rules. 

The much maligned ranged weapons rules are stupid, I agree, and were a seemingly lazy solution on the part of the designers to encourage people to engage the zombies in melee combat. I wish some official variant were approved (i.e. misses hit survivors) to satisfy players and provide a realistic justification for the rule, but in the end I still play with the rules as written, and the game works just fine.

RATING: 10
Excellent game for groups. Plays fine with 2-3 players as well as a full on 6. It's each to teach, and all the miniatures are fun to work with, especially showing it to people that have never played these large games before. It's expensive ,but well worth it. It's like playing an episode of The Walking Dead each time. With dozens more missions and characters on various websites you can download and print, this makes the the game that much more valuable. I really enjoy bringing this game out as a party game for strategists. Campaigns played so far have ranged from 1hr to 3.5hrs. Its thrilling working as a group to escape the game's scenarios. For larger games, once you run out of zombie miniatures, I have been using the counters from my card games (chessex 36 mini D6), otherwise the rules state all zombies get one extra move, which I don't think is quite fair since that relies on you just spending more money on extra zombies (expensive) to make sure that doesn't happen. I just assign a dice value for each zombie type and keep on playing. I've not had a bad time playing this game yet, even with a group of 4-5 friends ,all playing for 3 hours, and losing after all that time... it's still a blast to play.

RATING: 7
SOLO PLAY:

Fun Zombie survival Co-op. The more I play this one, the more I like it.

Set Up Notes:
-Set aside the following equipment cards: Evil Twins X1, Ma's Shotgu x1, and Molotov x2.
-No pregenenerated Zombies. The game does not have any any Zombies in play when the players take their first turn.

Rules Notes:
-Molotov are not found by searching, they are made by combining Gasoline and Bottle equipment cards.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
My favorite zombie game of all time!
I loved this game from the first play.
And I know it's flawed in some ways, but it's also amazing in so many more! I've got non-gamers into games with this as a gateway game so many times. They rush out and buy the next day.
Easy to teach. Clear and concise board. Video-game like player stats and player powers/level-ups. Fast paced, lots of cooperation and player interaction. Feels like you're in a zombie movie when the swarms of zombies come at you. So rewarding when you win! Lots of scenarios to play. Dice rolling works for me in this game only because zombies are so unpredictable, it feels right to be "rolling dice" to land a kill-shot/hit. You just never know if that hit did the zombie in or not.
Perfect game for zombies. And if you're not a zombie fan, you might be after playing this game.

RATING: 8
PROS
I really got the feeling we were fighting horde of zombies, for once! The fact you can really kill any of them with powerful weapons is very satisfying. I also liked the fact we could easily exchange weapons in order to balance players power (no weak player following behind the whole game.) Also, we had some freemdom: ie, we didn't have to stay on the exact same tile all of the game (as it was the case in Dark Darker Darkest).

CONS
On the downside, I don't feel we had that many choices along the way. Also, I'm worried the game might not have a huge replayability.

RATING: 8
It's not a brain busting puzzler, and it's not high drama. It's hordes of zombies coming at you in all their plastic glory while you frantically try to accomplish some goal and level up at the same time. The most interesting design choice is that leveling system, which increases skills from zero rapidly inside each scenario while racheting up the zombie just as fast. Go for skills by grabbing kills, or avoid to keep their numbers down?

RATING: 4
The zombies are coming!  The zombies are coming!

I am armed with a pan.  

Yes, when the apocalypse comes, I'll be Martha Stewart.  

And thus begins a series of very frustrating experiences with Zombicide.  With a pan, I have little chance to actually hit anything, but finding weapons is tough.  So I mostly trail around after the rest of my team-mates and try not to die.  The game's owner has an extra tray of zombies, but we still run out quickly, which gives the zombies an a bonus turn and makes things even more precarious for us.  And then there's the rule that if you use a ranged weapon in the same square as another player, you hit them, because we're all just that stupid.

(Look, I've never fired a gun in my life, but I have faith that if I were to do so right now, my friends would STAND BEHIND ME.  I'm not on the grassy knoll, people.  Bullets are not going to curve.)

Is this a game, or a thrown-together set of rules designed to sell minis?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Zombicide is definitely an enjoyable thematic romp. What is lacks in gameplay finesse, it more than makes up in theme. The game manages to convey a feeling of overwhelming odds better than any other cooperative game I've played. The sheer amount of zombies on the board combined with the fact that one mistake or miscalculation can be fatal makes it a real tightrope walk. Sure, there are some things that are less than perfect, such as the targeting rules and the possibility of an early player elimination - but all together Zombicide is so far the best zombie experience I've had in a board game form. Definitely recommended!

RATING: 6
Rules are moderately complex and the designers went for a simpler ruleset rather than complex rules to fit the theme. I don't mind the friendly fire rule, but don't like the added complexity of the actions dealing with vehicles. Scenario progression is nonlinear, which can be a good thing but I prefer a cohesive story. It is a lot of fun to throw a lot of dice and destroy a lot of zombies but the deep tactical play is not present.

Pros: Lots of decent quality miniatures. Huge scenario list, character list, and sandbox style design allows for custom scenario building. Kickstarter material not even missed. Simple to teach and play system. Different types of zombies introduce some variation in gameplay. Can play a wide number of players.

Cons: Some time needed to setup game, especially with more expansion material. Straightforward strategy and very little tactics. Fiddly rules with the later expansions. Scenarios run long.

RATING: 8.5
I was looking for a Zombie game based on the classic zombie scenario -

- Zombies was a bit too simplistic and the pvp didn't quite feel right.

- 'Last Night on Earth' seemed a bit straight-jacketed by it's scenarios, was handicapped by needing one player to play the zombies and I wasn't big on the art.

- 'Carnival Zombie' is good but it isn't the 'classic' zombie scenario/sandbox.

- Zpocalypse hasn't had great reviews

- Dawn of the Zeds (Second edition), sounds good but I believe it's based on the 'States of Seige' engine which is OK but a bit limited - wouldn't mind having a look at it though.

- I have 'Dead of Winter: A Crossroads Game' on the way but although it looks promising there isn't a whole lot of 'zombie' in it, I don't think. UPDATE - I was wrong there is quite a lot of 'zombie' in DoW but it is a slightly different take on the genre, so there is room for both.

So I went for Zombicide - 

Having now played Zombicide I'm definitely pleased with the purchase as it's a great zombie sandbox covering the all action part of the genre. The rules work fine out of the box but can easily be refined for your group's taste.

I'm not a big fan of the zombie amoeba splitting rule or the ranged targeting priority or the extra activation cards - all of which make the game (based on scenario 01 at least) silly hard. But the basic framework is flexible enough to easily accommodate house rules. I will be playing a few more times with the rules as written and then modifying to suit.

Great production values  - pretty sure this is the zombie game I was wanting.

RATING: 6
I think game succeeds brilliantly at what it sets out to do.  It is a fantastic production and has a nice clean ruleset.  It also avoids the trap of sticking one player with controlling the zombies like in Last Night on Earth.

A lot of people seem to complain about the targeting priority rules, but I actually think that is the most interesting part of the game.  You can't just run in your brawlers and stand back with your shooters.  Figuring out how to deal with that is the most tactically challenging aspect of the game.  

Ultimately, though, the game boils down to running up to zombies and rolling dice at them., which is too simplistic to hold my interest for long.  The expansions add some nice new features, but not really much depth.  This just isn't for me at this point in my gaming life.  

But man, does it look cool on the table!

RATING: 7.75
Zombicide is a customizable cooperative game set in a zombie apocalypse.  Players are survivors that are trying to find equipment, rescue other survivors, or making it to a shelter while avoiding the clutches of the mindless brain-hungry horde.  There are several preset scenarios that come with the game, or you can download a myriad of fan-made scenarios, or even make your own.  

Players make their way through a tile based city map to complete objectives and search for better equipment to deal with the zombie threat.  As players get more experience from killing zombies, the zombie spawns become increasingly difficult.  The action simulates a video game style as players upgrade their crowbars, pans, and pistols to rifles, shotguns, and chainsaws while the zombie body count rises.

In my experience Zombicide seems to plays best with 3 players controlling 2 survivors each because there is player elimination.  With 6 players, if your character dies there is little else for you to do.  Plus with fewer players it is easier to coordinate tactics than with a large group.  

Does Zombicide have the most elegant rules or tight gameplay?  No.  Are the dice-based combat and card-drawn zombie spawns highly luck based? Yes.  But despite that, my group and I have had a ton of fun taking on the horde and scrambling for our lives!  The game is highly customizable so you can easily make house rules, and come up with your own scenarios or campaigns.  Obviously this type of game isn't for everyone, but it's pretty clear what you're getting into just from the title itself.  If a zombie-themed, dice-rolling, tactical game of slaughter and survival sounds appealing, I'd recommend you give this one a look.

RATING: 10
UPDATE: I still love this game, and it might be one of my top dungeon crawl experiences, but I’ve decided that the base game and the first compendium is plenty for us. The expansions add a level of complexity that I don’t thing is needed.

UPDATE: One of the reasons I dropped Wizard Kings was because lack of scenarios to play. The Zombicide people know how to support their game after the fact.

Holy cow I love this game. Co-operative zombie slaying. Different characters, modular boards, and a plethora of missions make this one really replayable. I also like the mechanism that lets the zombies ramp up as you gain experience and skills -- it forces you to share the kills with the rest of the group.

I also have to give major kudos to the company for continued support: extra missions and characters are freely downloadable from their website as well as templates you make our own characters. 

I regret that I didn't know about the game to get in on the Kickstarter to get all the cool extras but I feel that I totally got my money's worth on this one.

RATING: 6
Out of the box, this game is a bit of a mess.  The components are great, but some of the rules are very anti-thematic and just plain odd.  Firing into a group of six zombies and a survivor and you're always going to hit the survivor first?  Zombies don't have to make any sort of roll to hit?  The only thing in the base game (which has tons of great looking minis and cards) that can kill an Abomination is a molotov cocktail....that's it?  Even two sawed-off shotguns with reload won't do it?  We didn't play a car scenario, but I've even read that you can shoot a passenger in the car with you while you're trying to shoot a zombie standing outside the car.  Sorry, but this kind of stuff completely takes me out of the theme.  Requires substantial house-rules to make it feel like a playtested Zombie game.  Really glad I didn't buy this game.

RATING: 6
Very amusing and truly a cooperative game, you need to go over the rules carefully and accept that it seems easy at the beginning because you missed something important. The various characters all have something they are "best" at, you need to use that skill constantly.

If you're a killing machine, survival is a secondary consideration.

The miniatures are much less impressive than they appeared on the kickstarter campaign, but I'd be lying if I didn't acknowledge they are above and beyond what most game pawns look like.

This may be the penultimate zombie game, but I'll happily play your copy.

Mall of Horror is better in my opinion, because the behavior and stress it elicits is less fun and more human.

Regardless, I cannot deny the appeal of wielding a chainsaw, wading into a zone full of the undead and giving them last rites.

RATING: 9.5
When I rate a game, its generally based on my enjoyment and perceived value. For me, Zombicide has been a huge win. A simple rule set, compelling decisions, and a great theme has kept it on the table for 10 straight plays in a row. I typically buy a game, play it once, maybe twice, and shelf it (sometimes permanently). This is one of the few games that has commanded repeat performances. There is a large number of additional missions available on the official Zombicide site. That, and the expansions which introduce new zeds (and thus require new strategies) should help keep this game fresh for a while. I passed over this one numerous times in the past due to the cost and unattainable exclusive Kickstarter content. Now, I'm sorry I did.

RATING: 3
A most basic cooperative game of Zombie hunting (or rather being hunted by Zombies; no, slowly being overwhelmed by ever-growing Zombie hordes). I like that they managed to keep the rules simple and intuitive for once, but unfortunately they are now so simple that there is nothing left to do for the players. The crucial decision points all hinge on either random dice rolls or random card draws, and the players can use their (hopefully) superior probability calculation skills to increase their odds in those endeavors.

"Why would you want to open that door? That will add approximately 15 more zombies to the board, and if we just stick to the road, we'll be out of the city in about 5 turns." "But, but... if we don't go into the house we won't be able to find stuff!"

In the words of one of those players who actually seem to like the game the problem with the short scenarios is that they are "just not interesting." The problem with the longer scenarios, of course, is that they are long. Very long. With not an interesting decision in sight. Oh please, dear zombies, just kill me now.

RATING: 10
So many excellent missions. So easy to play with an uncomplicated rule set. Every scenario changes each time you play it, no 2 sessions are ever the same. Play the same mission with different players and the game changes due to personalities.

Hundreds of official and fan made missions and gaming night campaigns. Also very easy to create your own missions, campaigns and scenarios from a simple set of tokens.

Additional sets for expansion, buy more characters, or have fun creating your own custom characters from blank player cards.

Add companions and dogs to make it easier, add more zombies or zombie dogz or crows to make it truly horrifyingly hard.
 
10 out of 10 :-)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Don't buy [b][i]Zombicide[/i][/b] expecting a refined ruleset (the rules initially needed some work, though Guillotine Games has issued a v3 that is pretty solid). Don't buy it if you want a cheap game (it's expensive and loaded with high-quality plastic figures). Definitely do not buy this game if you want to optimize an economic engine. Instead, buy this game because it feels like a zombie game should feel: Hectic, fast, and dangerous. 

Having to perform bookkeeping (which plagues many thematic games and washes them of their flavor) during a zombie apocalypse would be truly asinine. Fortunately Zombicide--with its simple rules, clever kill trackers, and waves of undead--feels like a zombie apocalypse. Better yet, the different missions with deep and changing strategy makes for a fun board game.

◊s◊

RATING: 7
It is a tense but fun game. I am still trying to play all the missions but I don't have many gaming sessions. For the first 5 missions, the most difficult have been No. 2 and 5, we have died on those, and I just had one victory on no. 2.

We play with a house rule, where each player can make his actions simultaneously with other players, so the cooperation aspect of the game is reinforced.

Also we use a rule to force rooms to get empty after a player draws a food or Argh card. This forces the players to explore.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Being a huge zombie fan I've spend a lot of money and time searching for the best zombie boardgame.. Zombicide is exactly that, no less.. Since I've bumped into the first Kickstarter for Zombicide last year by accident, my friends and I have played it more than 20 times. Thus It quickly replaced all other boardgames I used to have.

The games simplicity yet strategy based rules will have players returning to the game again and again. Even people I know who dislike zombies, and boardgames have still joined in on the frenzy zombie madness and kept coming back for more.

The fact that the GG have shown so much loyalty to their fans and still keeps feeding us with new missions, will assure that we never have had to play the same mission twice.

Cons:

Great game, lots of fun with the right group.

RATING: 9
Not without a few flaws but overall, amazing fun. Enough tactics with tense moments and lots of dice and luck thrown in. Simple yet superbly engaging. Now with unbelievable amounts of content to add or leave out, at your whim and want. Maybe a minor tweak for balance next time is all you will need for creating wild changes to the system. Very cool.

This is maybe the most cinematic game i own, and it rewards you with a crazy roller coaster tale every time. Even when playing solo, it never misses a beat. This, and more, helps make the game a top 5 title hands down. 
It has to lose some marks for that age old problem, i.e: for scenario, read: Puzzle. ala space hulk etc. 
But unlike many games with this type of map making, Z'cide is so immersive, win or lose. You often get swept along in the fun and panic, so much so in fact, that you forgot you could have maybe puzzle solved your way out of it.

Bought Toxic City Mall after a little, "what should i buy next" research.
After which, I got on the final KS for the experience.
My season 3 KS arrived. This was the biggest pile of 'stuff' I have ever seen.
I didn't know what to do with the plastic mountain for the longest time, I either had to embrace what I had, or sell the lot.
After a couple of games with my 9 yr old lad, who absolutely loved it (his 2nd favorite behind Talisman, I'm told), I've decided to embrace it.

I have spent a good few quid on Z'cide, but I never feel the need to own every last little thing. Luckily i left that illogical completionist nonsense far behind me many moons ago. I will possibly buy one or two after market minis, but i will have to really want them, i am in no hurry, and it will have to be at a very  sensible price. So probably never. The retail shelf stuff gives you more than a lifetimes worth for 1 game out of, no doubt many games on your shelf anyhoo.
So far I have bought aftermarket: Bill from ebay in america for less than 8 quid inc postage. Swerengen is a favorite tv character of mine, so i had him on ebay alert, it was cheaper to get him sent across the pond than pay any UK hawkers price. 
Plus, I got the puke green dice for a tenner, as a bit of fun for my son. 
Both overpriced, in my book, but it's not going too mad. Not a lot else interests me enough to pay over the odds for really. You can usually find a mini amongst all the retail kit, that resembles the pose of who you want to proxy easily enough. Only a huge lottery win could tempt me to want any 1st ed exclusives etc on the open market.

I have just sold a pile of games so had a little dabble into 2nd hand prison outbreak territory. 
Seems many prefer the equipment deck, there are some neat survivors, berserkers are popular, and I would definitely like to play as Grindlock!

Well, now we are pretty organised. We know what we have, and pretty much, what we like to mix in.
So me and my lad will be having a blast with the system. Even if he doesn't get the sub MG's & Chainsaw every game.....so he says! 
"You have the pan dad". 

Good times.

RATING: 7
Zombicide is a tactical minis game about survivors killing zombies. It has a modular board, various scenarios, and heroes with different special abilities. Heroes can spend their turn searching for items in buildings (but not outside) and will be forced to fight any Zombies in their space. So far, everything I've said could also be said of Last Night on Earth. It seems a virtual certainty that Zombicide took a lot of influence from this earlier game. 

So what are the differences? Well, the main one is that Zombicide is a pure co-op, where the zombies are automatically controlled by certain rules. Another is that the more experience the heroes have, the tougher the zombie outbreaks become. Lastly, noise is a factor; firing a gun may attract more Zombies (and noise can even be used in your favor). 

One of the complaints some people have about Last Night on Earth is that the zombie player doesn't have as many interesting decisions as the hero players do. This is true from the perspective of tactical positioning, but the zombie player also has many more cards in hand to work with, so I personally think they are just "different", not less interesting. I also strongly prefer competitive games to co-operative ones. In light of that, this game, while a lot of fun, seems very redundant to me. 

Last Night on Earth has shown that it is primarily a "toolkit" kind of game. It would be very possible to make a purely co-operative scenario by cranking up the difficulty of the zombies. It would also be possible to have scenario rules for noise. Consequently, this game feels to me like playing someone's homemade scenario for Last Night on Earth, rather than a game unto itself. Since I love Last Night on Earth, this isn't necessarily a drawback, but I can't help feeling that this game is much more limited in its capabilities to come up with interesting scenarios. I just can't see a lot of reason to play this over Last Night on Earth, though it is a lot of fun.

RATING: 8
It's over expensive, I don't like the heroes sculpts that much; some people are exhilarated by them, but I do prefer the heroes of LNOE; the zombies sculps are better and more varied, but yet do not justify the price tag; there are much much better zombies minis available.
The tiles are double faced but all buildings amount to the same; they lack variety.

But, unlike LNOE, everybody plays survivors and the game plays much faster; it lacks the variety introduced by the cards in LNOE, but the system is much more fluid. 
It feels more tactical, and also the story told, even if it lacks the story elements and dark humor introduced by the decks of LNOE, feels more true to the zombie genre and more verisimilar.

The game takes significantly longer than expected, but the action isgripping enough so it does not feel long to me.

In summary it's an overpriced good zombie game caracterized by a clean and streamlined design, and largely succeeds in recreating the mood and atmosphere of zombie flicks.

RATING: 7
This game does a FANTASTIC job of simulating the feel of a zombie-filled world. The more time you spend, noise you make, etc... the more zombies come for you! The last desperate moments of each game spent running and hacking and slashing and shooting your way to the mission objective (maybe even sacrificing a brave soul in the process) are priceless. 

The board and minis are top-notch, and the box has great storage for them all. 

All that said, the game grows pretty stale after awhile. There simply isn't enough variety in the base game to keep things interesting after a few plays and the various scenarios don't feel different enough from each other.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This game makes the zombie theme come alive! This is a total Ameritrash game, but it is so well done. You and a group of at least four other people will need to cut out a whole evenings worth of gaming for just one sitting of Zombicide. But it's worth it! This is a coop game, but it's not like your usual coops. If one person dies, the game is not over. There are different objectives in each mission and as long as one person makes it to the end...you win.

It is so fun watching the horde of zombie's grow! The miniature quality of this game is excellent. Player boards and artwork are superb. It does have a few rules that don't make sense that you might want to house rule. For example, when firing a gun into a zone with zombie's and your friends....it says you automatically hit your friends first. You might want to change that because this game is HARD as it is!

One of the reasons this was such a hit was because of how you learn the game. Rather than sitting down and having someone bombard you with all the rules and nuances of the game; this rulebook has a tutorial mission where you learn all the different mechanics and how all the basics work. It only takes about 20 minutes or so to go through it.

RATING: 8
A really fun dice-fest.  Purely cooperative game with a nice mix of strategy and tactics requiring teamwork, all wrapped up in a zombie-slaying genre.  Fun for gamers and non-gamers alike.  The time flies by when playing.  

Unfortunately the game has some balance issues... like several scenarios that are far too easy or far too difficult (impossible?) as written, and various overpowered strategies (e.g. car exploitation, pass the chainsaw, etc).  It feels like some brief playtesting would have caught many of these issues... like the designers had tested 3 or 4 scenarios, then made up 6 or 7 more (without testing them) to fill up the rule book.

Backed on Kickstarter, May 2012.  Arrived September 2012.  Have full "Abomination package" with extra tray of zombies, extra Abomination, 9 survivors (6 more coming in 2013, plus their zombie versions), extra sets of dice (18 custom dice in 3 colours), extra tile set, signed lithograph, T-shirt.  I've painted the heroes and am working on the zombies.  I also customized the player boards and some of the cards, and made a custom goalie mask.

RATING: 8.62
Just the zombie game I was looking for. Not one or two lone walkers but a board full of the undead looking to remove the brains of my would-be heroes. 
It's very easy to learn and relatively quick to play. A game always starts slow but ends up an opus of blood, gore and flying corpses before long. There are few gaming moments as satisfying as mowing down a dozen undead in a single turn. Can't wait to track myself down a copy of Zombicide Season 2. 
Happy Halloween everyone! (^_^)

RATING: 6
Zombicide is one of the better zombie-themed games I've played. It's got a fast-pace and is a rare exception to my dislike of combat resolved by dice rolls (mostly because combat happens frequently, slightly offsetting a bad roll or two).

It does, however, have player elimination without the guarantee of a quick finish after the first elimination.

It's not a game that will probably ever end up in my collection only because of the miniatures driving up the price. I'm not a fan of painting them - I'd rather have some sort of other piece to represent characters and zombies.

RATING: 6
Yeah, it has some really bizarre rules, but [i]they work[/i], and they don't detract from the overall fun of the game.

So what if firing into a group hits the Survivors first? Then [i]don't fire into a group[/i]. Problem solved.

Has some randomness issues, but seems pretty well balanced. It can be a really tough game to beat, but even if you lose you have fun doing it.

Edit: After 10 plays I have found my interest in this game waning. I would prefer something a little more strategic in a zombie game: this is the part that gives intrigue to [i]The Walking Dead[/i] and other zombie movies. A whole movie that was about nothing but blasting zombies would not be interesting (not to me, anyway). A whole game about it is also not very interesting.

RATING: 4
2013-01-23

Initial Rating: 5.0 (January 2013)

I love zombie games so I was keen on trying Zombicide. My first play was hugely disappointing, but that was due to a big mistake on the rules (zombies never appeared in buildings) made by the explainer. My second game was much more enjoyable. 

The game components are superb, the zombie minis are great and the scenarios are very fun to play. I also like that the game is pretty hard to win, until now, no one in my game group has been able to successfully finish a mission (without rules mistakes).  The game is very fluid so it generally plays relatively quickly (perhaps because we died so often). More important, the downtime is very short. 

On the bad side the game is pretty expensive, I’m not sure if I want to spend that kind of money on this game (although I probably will). The player boards seemed like a good idea at the beginning, but managing the player`s inventory in the board is a minor pain in the ass. A friend made some better boards and we are using them instead. Also there is a hero mini (Phil) that constantly is mistaken by a zombie and in one game a player attacked it :Devil: It needs to be painted ASAP.

Bottom line a good zombie game. I will upgrade its rating to a 6.5. This is not a game I want to play all the time but it is a game I enjoy. I still prefer to play LNOE because a player can control the zombies, but Zombicide is a lot more tactical than LNOE and that is important to me.
 
Current rating: 6.5

2013-05-30

I almost never want to play Zombicide and, in general, I like Zombie games :S. 

After a couple of plays, the game is very boring for me. Lots of luck and obvious decisions, not a Co Op I like. Also with all the add-ons (expansions, promos, etc.) Zombicide is Uber expensive, what a money pit, with this kind of money I could buy several (better) games. I’m glad I didn’t buy it.

The redeeming factor are the gorgeous miniatures, but still that is not enough for me to play the game. 

I’m downgrading its rating so it matches my new feelings for the game. If the Zombie mood strikes, I would play Last Night on Earth instead.

RATING: 9
Love it.  It has quickly become my favorite Ameritrash game- and if you know me, you know I often do not care for Ameritrash style games, so when I say I "love" this game after two plays, it says a lot.  

The production values are good; not great.  They work and they work because of scale and quantity.  I do like the tiles and the amount of detail added, as well.

  Everything has been worked out mechanically to be simple and smooth, even though there are some things that don't exactly makes sense (e.g. splitting zombies, targeting priority), but I can see why they are done this way, and it is for the greater good of the game and ultimately serves the tension the game seeks to produce.   

This is as close to a true zombie apocalypse game as there can be, I think, giving a very cooperative feel that players must work together and protect each other from making poor choices that may lead to bad consequences for everyone(e.g., the leveling up system or opening certain doors).  Therefore, its coop, but with this palpable sense of dread the whole way through.  

Again, this is great stuff.  I'll never need to own another zombie game (other than City of Horror, which is less about zombies and more about negotiation).

RATING: 1
Move, move, search. "I found a pan!" search "Another pan!" move, move. Trade pan for pistol. Move, shoot, miss, shoot, hit. Activate zombies....(5 minutes later)...

I really can't think of any redeeming qualities for this game. Somebody always gets screwed with a bad character. Somebody always gets screwed with crappy weapons. Somebody always gets screwed with never being able to kill any zombies to level up their character. Fiddlieness and upkeep are awful. You have to place noise tokens every time a gun is fired or a door opened. Then you have to spawn zombies and figure out what types go where. Then you have to move all the zombies on the board according to their type. And any time you open a door to a building you have to spawn zombies AGAIN in every room of the building. And if that isn't enough, someone is going to be quarterbacking the whole game. It's really just rolling dice for 3 hours listening to someone else tell the team what they should do. 

I could probably be talked into trying the new Zombicide Black Plague but I'm not holding my breath to play it. For now if you are looking for a zombie game with dice rolling then I would recommend Run, Fight, or Die!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The game suffers from some serious flaws.  #1: early player elimination.  #2: game is heavily based on luck (die rolls in combat, card draws), #3: game penalizes you for making progress (benefits of entering yellow and orange greatly outweighed by penalty of increased # and strength of placed zombies), and #4: combat rules, especially ranged, detract from theme and enjoyment of the game (attach heroes first?).   My biases: I generally do not enjoy cooperative games as much, and I can take or leave the zombie themed games (I enjoy Last Night on Earth a little more).

RATING: N/A
Zombicide is a collaborative game in which players take the role of a survivor – each with unique abilities – and harness both their skills and the power of teamwork against the hordes of unthinking undead! Zombies are predictable, stupid but deadly, controlled by simple rules and a deck of cards. Unfortunately for you, there are a LOT more zombies than you have bullets.

Find weapons, kill zombies. The more zombies you kill, the more skilled you get; the more skilled you get, the more zombies appear. The only way out is zombicide!

Play ten scenarios on different maps made from the included modular map tiles, download new scenarios from the designer's website, or create your own!

RATING: 8
Essentially "Left 4 Dead: The Boardgame". Fast-paced, crazy and zany, RPG-esque -- just a ton of gory, unapologetic fun. Your character grows stronger and stronger, while the hoards grow bigger and hungrier... soon your mowing them down by the dozen while your teammates sprint for the last objective and the Abomination is stomping right behind you...

Very easy to pick up, awesome co-op experience, tons of variability with the modular board, fantastic components, simple mechanics. It's not the most strategic game, and random chance plays a large role (lots of dice rolls) but it's always a blast.

See "Black Plague" for the most refined version of the game (and adopt its ruleset for this version if you like the modern theme better)

RATING: 9
I love this game. I prefer a modern setting for Zombie games and Zombicide really set the bar high. The game isn't perfect but, IMO, can be house ruled to perfection. You can easily take many of the changes that they made to the formula in Black Plague and apply them easily. My ONLY complaint is the tiles are kind of bendy. I live in a pretty dry area and still see some warping sometimes. They bend back into place easily enough but sometimes start to re-bend while playing which can be annoying. I suggest getting the Walking Dead All Out War Scenery Expansion from Mantic Games to add to Zombicide and the only CMON expansion I think is really worth it is the Zombie Dogs. They increase the difficulty a bit and really add pressure to the game at unexpected moments.

RATING: 6
([url=http://www.kickstarter.com/projects/coolminiornot/zombicide]www.kickstarter.com[/url], with Abomination pack,  received on 2012-08-28)

Zombicide has great qualities for a zombie game, but is also overrated. The minis are great, but the game tiles are pretty bad. The colors are weak, and the material is cheap. Thick but can easily be damaged. The tokens also are pretty bland. The game itself can be really fun, but doesn't scale well for less than 5 players. Kept around 90 minutes, it's a nice experience. Anything above is painfully repetitive. The gameplay is simple for a quick dice rolling based fignthing game, there are lots of missions, and I highly praise Guillotine Games for supporting the game with tons of online content. However, based on gameplay alone, cost I spent for the game and resell value, I had to get rid of it for a 100% profit.

(Sold to user [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/user/francki]francki[/url])

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
This is a mediocre-though-sometimes-fun game that could be so much more enjoyable if you got to make more interesting decisions and if had benefited from more development time. A few thrilling moments can't make up for the rest of the moments.

The rulebook is sloppy and includes some poor decisions, and the scenarios are apparently in reverse or mixed-up order: #1 is easily one of the hardest, and #10 is a cakewalk. They skimped on the boards (reproducing the same or very nearly the same graphics multiple times feels cheap in a game with such cool minis and this kind of price tag), the character cards are too flimsy to handle sliding the kill marker without moving around all the item cards on them, and the zombie cards make it hard to tell zombies apart. The minis are the big draw, but it feels rushed to print in so many other ways. 

Having spent my first game failing most rolls and not doing much of anything for three hours, I see the potential for that happening again in subsequent games. If one person gets a couple of lucky draws, their ability to rack up kills and level up increases dramatically, while the schlubs get to schlub along. Fuck that noise.

Despite my first game taking three fucking hours, not being much fun, and ending in failure because the first scenario is insane and painful with four players/four characters, I played it a second time. We applied the tweak of having a minimum of six characters (or six lives spread among however many you have), and it made a big difference.

There's a fun game hiding under all the sloppiness and boredom, but it's too well-hidden for me to ever want to see this again. I love zombies and I wanted to like this, but I don't.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
This feels like you're in a zombie apocalypse, and I love it!  I think they really captured how zombies would act (with the noise mechanic, quite clever in my opinion).  The difficulty and randomness of the game actually lend themselves to the overall idea and theme as well: zombies are literally everywhere, your chances of survival slim, if you don't stick very closely together, you WILL lose.

The quality of the game pieces, especially the minis, is very high.  I think the replayability is also very high if you factor in the customization in scenarios and the board that are available.  You can really make it your own game.

Highly recommend to everyone who is a pulp zombie movie fan and loves an excellently executed co-op game.

Added 8/18/2014: Something to keep in mind is that this game is more of a run and gun zombie movie or video game (think Left 4 Dead) as opposed to a zombie survival scenario (a la The Walking Dead).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/949829/zombicide-a-single-playersolo-review/page/1

Santa 2013

Nice thing to have. If you're ok with Amert games, are ok with modern interpretations of Zombies and want a cooperative then this is it; if you prefer traditional (proper zombies or at least proper zombie films) and want pvp then LNOE is the one (both good games).

Not wild about games getting more expensive but in this case it's fair enough - lots of high quality bits, although I would strongly prefer larger cards.

Mechanicly, despite my criticisms of the lack of them during much of the original KS, the rule set is good and delivers arcade fun, somehow more so than LNOE IMHO. The much maligned 'hit allies if shooting into squares with them' rule while perhaps irritating does add a significant amount of strategic and tactical scope to the game so no complaints here (simply a great rule :thumbsup:). Another common complaint is that the game is overly susceptible to one player calling all of the shot - frankly this is an external problem just don't play with that player.

Decision wise it is what it is. If you want a Zombie game here's a worthy one, if you want a game with deep decision making then look further. Nice game that gives you a dungeon crawler-esq gameplay with some added unique mechanics and the feel of 29 days later survival experience. 

I've added in another box of Zombies (set #1) and Toxic City Mall and think I'm now finished buying stuff from this series, I may be wrong, but will definitely continue to enjoy playing it for years to come.

(Pretty sure in time this will become a grail game.)

RATING: 10
What an amazing sandbox of Ameritrashy (Français-déchets?), dicefesty, cheap-thrilly, goretastic goodness.

*Ahem* There are great opportunities for team tactics and strategy, its got satisfying social interaction, and its (usually) quite challenging.

My group has modified the vanilla game into an entirely different animal, but the game itself begs to be tuned to each individual group's liking. This is not to say I don't think the rules as presented are playable (Myth, anyone?), just a bit clunky.

There are a ton of available additives and preservatives for Zombicide (I've got most), but I admit I'm still waiting for an expansion that adds something genuinely new to the experience rather than adding so much more of the same. This is one of my TOP TEN games, but I love mashed potatoes too, and all the Zombicide seasons are starting to feel like a three course meal of nothing but mashed potatoes with mashed potatoes for dessert. Ah, why am I whining? This game is so fun!

RATING: 7
Recently purchased after backing the kickstarter for season 2. 

After the first play I really want to play again soon, might take on a scenario solo. 

Game lends itself to house ruling a couple things to make certain elements make more sense but these might make gameplay too easy or too difficult but I am yet to really be able to tell.

House Rules Implemented:
Shooting in close combat ignores ranged rules. All other shooting if zombies missed roll second time to see if human hit on a 4+.
Turn order. Players took turns taking actions with one survivor each back and forth instead of all survivors controlled by the player. Switching starting player each turn.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.7
I was a Kickstarter backer for this one, but to 'sell' it to Mrs Fish I presented it as a Xmas present for myself - "Look dear, no shopping and no more to pay. All we have to do is wrap it and I'm sorted for Saturnalia". I got away with it too!

We have managed six plays so far and are really enjoying it. I like the theme and the components are top notch. The miniatures are really well sculpted, both characters and zombies. The modular mapboards are suitably atmospheric and the counters, character boards and suchlike are durable and thoroughly fit-for-purpose. The extra dice that came with the Kickstarter sets are also rather fun. The only negative is that the cards are a bit small and fiddly, but that’s something I can live with.

 I am a big Last Night on Earth: The Zombie Game fan as well, but when it's just the two of us it rarely hits the table. As Mrs Fish enjoys co-operative games, she likes a game or three of Pandemic, she was willing to try this one and has even (once) asked to play it over our other 'staples' of Agricola and Race for the Galaxy.

So, having established that the production values are very good and the theme is to my liking and, possibly more importantly, the game will get played in the House of Fish the next question should be about gameplay. I quite like the way it plays, it's reasonably simple to pick up and the game system is very good as a co-operative. That there are four different types of zombies is also good both for the sheer joy of variety as well as the different challenges each sort poses. The most common are ‘walkers’ familiar from the George A Romero films, they shamble on mindlessly, but what they lack in ability they make up for in numbers and can swamp the heroes if given the chance. Then there are ‘runners’ they move twice as quickly and can ruin the best laid plans as they divert the player’s attention away from that they should be doing to dealing with these sprinters. The ‘fatties’ present their own challenges in that not every weapon can kill them, and the abomination is just plain old bad news as it is invulnerable to everything except molatovs – and no-one starts the game with one of those. 

There are a few 'gamey' bits that I don't particularly like, but understand such as trying to explore houses and suchlike while the characters are all still rookies as this level generates fewer zombies (usually - the game we played last night saw an abomination - the toughest of the zombie types – turn up while we were all still on the stating level of experience) but in most non-adversarial game there are always ways to ‘game’ the system.

Other things can be a bit silly such as being able to search a car while in another car. Most of this can be ignored or worked around. Where it excels in design is the use of noise tokens. This adds a tactical element to the game which I really enjoy in that the players can attempt to use the noise they generate doing things like shooting, smashing open doors or even just breathing to manipulate the movement of the zombies and get them away from the areas the heroes need to go to in order to complete their mission.

This is not to say that zombie movement is totally predictable, it can always go a bit wrong, especially when another activation cards is drawn – especially for the runners who move double the rate of everything else. So, plenty of tactical decisions to make as well as an element of unpredictability which can make for some tense and exciting gameplay.

Another plus is that Guillotine Games provide some excellent on-line support for this game with over a dozen new scenarios available on their website was well as version 1.0 of FAQs.

Guillotine Games have also announced that the first expansion will be published when the second batch of Kickstarter stuff (mainly extra characters) ships out around March/April this year.

Looking forward to both!

RATING: 7.6

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I can kind of see what all the hype is about with this one but I don't personally rate it as high as the lovers do. Its ok but there's plenty of other games I'd play instead given the chance.

What is good? The production qualities are high, the miniatures are beautiful and the tiles (whilst a bit lazily repetitive with No.4's wheelie bin on every road) are big and nice looking. In fact the minis and tiles are SO good I am tempted to get a copy of the game just to tear up the rulebook and use the components for the tactical miniatures game 'All Things Zombie' which is a great system but doesn't have any of its own minis/terrain.

The bad is that the game itself just feels a bit dry and just doesn't pull me in at all. Its very gamey, with odd rules that take you right out of the thematic feeling for the sake of playing straight. Not being able to shoot into other players spaces or drive through them without hitting the players first is silly and could have been implemented better. I also cringe every time 'zombie mitosis' occurs to a zombie with two equal routes to travel. Also there is too many Zombies down manholes in this game!

This one can also be gamed like a bitch- you can often spend several turns stood together waiting for Zeds to funnel in behind you so you can move out of the opposite end of the building. Clever, but totally unthematic. If you all stood in a building and made no noise the Zeds would surely just mill about where they lost track of you..

There's also just too many Zombies (and running ones at that). It usually gets to the point where there is so many spawning that you can't move for several turns for simply killing the front of the que before you are eventually overwhelmed.

I remember when Zombie themed stuff was about suspense and dread (like the original Night of the Dead movie and Resident Evil games), and how one zombie could be really dangerous, let alone 2 or 3! Nowadays there is an obsession for Zombie stuff having 1000s of Zombies that can be easily killed. Its not that its bad, just...meh.

While its still a bar above Zombies!!! at the same time the Coop feature sucks a lot of the fun for me. Zombicide punishes you for thinking and acting on your own. All players are forced to carefully plan their every move as a group because dying is incredibly easy and happens fast if you split up. This makes it great for solitaire play, but pretty lame for Coop as most of the time the group is controlling your character and not you.

Production qualities aside, I personally think Last Night on Earth is better as a Zombie game, even with its oddities and over bloating from too many expansions. Zombicide is no less bloated now I mention it! Toxic zombies, berserker zombies, crawling zombies, dogs, crows, the list goes on, but when will it stop?..

RATING: 6
El primer juego medianamente bueno de zombis. Es un Pandemic de 3 horas con dados. Tienen una buena base para hacer el juego de zombis definitivo si mejoran el tema del sonido, que suena muy bien pero en la practica sirve de poco ya que casi siempre te ven y se pierde esa parte estratégica. Y ese punto de que en cualquier momento se lía y te matan sin remedio está muy bien en un juego de 45 minutos como Pandemic pero en uno de 3 horas no hace tanta gracia. La eliminación de jugadores, comprensible en un juego con esta temática pero muy molesta.

RATING: 5

So, just for the fun of killing cool zombies.

*********************************
After a couple of games:
-> Big con: you have to avoid leveling up!!!
-> The miniatures are cool, but not as cool as the seemed in the promo material.
-> At the end, you end up doing a lot of metagaming as strategy (killing zombies just to avoid depleting them: one you deplete the zombies, they move double and this is most likely to mean deaths for all players).
-> There are some rules, like the double move, that ruin the strategy.

Still, the powers are cool and the game is better balanced than I expected. I would not mind playing from time to time, but I will never be a fan or buy it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.25
This game is ok, but nothing spectacular.  The theme is well implemented but the gameplay isn't very deep.  Basically, you are running around an urban landscape during a zombie outbreak.  You can move, attack or search for new equipment.  Your characters level up over the course of the game, but there is no campaign mode in the base game.

Some features of this game are:
- co-operative, no hidden information and plays solitaire
- fairly simple rules but the rule book is not as clear as it should be
- nice miniatures and other components
- not a lot of different weapons or other loot in the base game
- lots of dice rolling, so understanding odds and accepting luck is necessary
-as long as one player knows the rules, you can get into the action pretty quickly
- each character has some kind of unique skill or ability and as they level up they receive new abilities
- the game doesn't attempt to balance difficulty with the number of players, so it's best to just play with 6 characters no matter how many people are playing

I'm sure a lot could be done with this system to make it more interesting, but the base game itself isn't something I'd care to play very often.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
When I first purchased this game, it was my favourite. I loved the theme, the setting, all the neat items and the artwork. I'd push and promote the game on all my friends,  but after several plays, the game just doesn’t pass as a game to me. It almost feels like it started out as a collectible pack that someone who has only played one or two board games decided to turn into a game. 

Why? 
(1) One item deck for every room. 
(2) Survivor-First Target Priority.
(3) Useless items that can’t be combined into something more useful.

All of those make for an extremely un-thematic experience, (2) being the worst. Of all the ways ranged weapons could have been balanced, that is by far the strangest. 


What might work better?
(1) Different decks for different types of rooms with limited searches. (eg. Garage/Mechanical = +% Gasoline cans)  
(2) Dual-sided Ammo/Noise tokens that would limit the Survivor from just range-ing everything. 
(3) Combining edible items to create Healing items. Cliché, but better than hauling around a bag of rice.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Zombie Hoards! This is the closest thing yet to playing Left 4 Dead in board game format. The components are fantastic, the box storage is excellent and protects the minis well. The board looks awesome. This is quick to learn and easy to remember rules. This game is great for new or casual gamers. We have had some "not so interested in playing a board game" people over, and we have hooked them into playing board games completely and solely based on this board game! Sometimes the game can feel too easy, but then I remember that killing zombies should be fun. But on the other hand there are plenty of scenarios that will kick you when you are down...hard and beyond! Spinning around in a circle with a chain saw and taking out ferocious zombies hoarding around you...now that is classic Left 4 Dead stuff! This game can have you whooping and hollering when your character(s) are seemingly surrounded in a no-win situation...and all of a sudden one character decides to pull out the duel sub-machine guns to save the day. Or maybe you find an abandoned car, jump in and mow down an oncoming hoard of walkers. Take that you zombie scum!

Some of the best features of the game are the zombie split. This can be devastating and can catch you with your pants down. When a zombie is equidistant to 2 locations an equal number of zombies must go in both locations (thus adding new zombies, unexpectadly to the board). Another great feature, is the experience meter. As you kill zombies, your experience goes up with each kill. Thus moving you into the more dangerous yellow, orange and deadly red zombie spawning danger zones. 

If there is anything we learned in Left 4 Dead it's...stick together! There is so much interaction...so much table talk...laughter...whooping for joy...morning the loss of a pet dog...discussion...tactical thinking...that this game is such a thrill to play! Anytime we have a game night...this game is mentioned and it is hard to resist playing.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A neat co-op with simple rules which mesh thematically nicely with the simple beasts that keep on coming. Lots of different scenarios, but basically you have 3 actions with which to move, shoot (dice rolling) or get a card which will generally provide ongoing item-type benefits. What makes this a bit different is that the zombies don't fight. They have a search algorithm to come after you, and if your turn ends with a zombie on your space, you're taking a wound. Two wounds and you're kaput. And moving off a space requires an extra action for each zombie on that space. So if you get cornered and fail to shoot your way out of there by rolling well, you could be inundated. Nicely thematic. Meaning the game does actually require you to plan and co-ordinate with your fellows. There's randomness in the spawning, there's randomness in the shooting - manage it as best you can. It comes in at the right length. Fun all round.

RATING: 5
Played once on a medium scenario and found many aspects to be really fun (i.e. seeing a horde of zombies marching down a street towards your dwindling band of people is pretty great), but would probably be hesitant to play again. Obviously wasn't play tested that well and some aspects of the game are just totally ridiculous. For instance, (1) unlimited searching per room. A little more balanced progression would have been nice.

Totally overrated in my opinion.

RATING: 6.5
I've downgraded this from a 9 (what was I thinking!) to a 6.5. I loved Zombicide when it came out but after 6 plays or so it's soooooo boring. There are no real meaningful decisions because usually the board starts filling up with zombies and they force you to take a certain path if you want to survive. You very rarely get the chance to upgrade your character's skills because you will most likely win before then. The minis and components are excellent but I feel like the game is too easy and that there's always an obvious choice. 

The game is an excellent gateway though. New people always love it and it's simple enough for them to understand. It gives the illusion of choice for people who aren't experienced. I don't particularly want to play again but I know I will have to. My game group doesn't seem to want to play anything else :(

RATING: 7
Pretty solid zombie game with a simple and enjoyable system.  Maps are big and clear and cool, and the level of monotonous chaos caused by card play is fair and sensible (not like "Last Night on Earth", where I felt the card play made even short-term strategy pretty useless).  The noise markers are a clever touch, and the fact that it is wholly cooperative (with some surprises in the "spawn" draw) make it more fun than LNoE and just as interesting without the frustrating trump cards. Plus, characters improve with experience in a simple, but cool way. Rating based on one play (The Big W scenario), where we won after Ned cleared a critical intersection with a molotov cocktail.  I'm pretty impressed so far, and am eager to see what other scenarios are like.

[floatleft][ImageID=1303633][/floatleft][b][u]Initial Impressions:[/u][/b]
As a personal rule of thumb I strongly dislike almost all Ameritrash type games. Of course there is always an exception to the rule and Zombicide is definitely one of those exceptions. I really enjoy Zombicide for what it is.
