RATING: 7.4
Very well themed, it almost plays like RPG, with players naturally describing what the party of survivors is doing, adding gore details and sound effects.  It is also quite simple to explain, and the flat co-operative nature of the game allows new players to jump into the action quickly, being fed the details they need along the game.

The game is designed to be hacked, and in my club we have tons of house rules, for example.

Because of the full co-op mechanics, one possible drawback is that it is very easy to inadvertently exclude somebody from the action, if the group of players is not attentive to include everybody into the discussion/decision making at each turn.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Mechanically decent coop, which like many both suffers and benefits from an Alpha player. Manages to look like the situation is hopeless, then the team rallies and turns it round. However, just doesn't 'do it' for me... I couldn't care less about the characters or the zombies.

RATING: 5.5
This game feels like quite a few rules were added at the last minute for balance. Many of these take away from the theme, and I think theme is important for zombie survival games. 

Some examples: 

if you shoot a ranged weapon into a tile with a human player you will hit them every time -- regardless of the number of zombies in that tile. 

If zombies have two equal paths to travel they will split into two and travel both ways. 

I found myself saying "I don't want to move to space A because the zombies will split, I'll run out of miniatures sooner, and the zombies will get extra activations". It works for balance, but it kinda kills the theme for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I'm going to put this right at the top. The two most important things to know about this game:
* The only rule is to have fun. Every other rule can be tweaked. It's a sandbox, but unlike some sandbox games, it starts out with a really great set of rules and lets you tweak from there.
* You don't need any of the kickstarter exclusives. They really don't add anything to the game. The exclusive minis have no game changing features and the exclusive survivor dashboards can be printed out or you'll find even more interesting ways to make up your own survivors. You don't need it. If you're like me and you feel a strong compulsion for completionism, it might interest you to know that by the time I'd played my 2nd game of Zombicide, I had learned enough about the game to no longer have any interest in the exclusives.

Pros:
* Fun, tense, exciting. It's really a blast to play this game. It starts out slow, but just a few turns in you're going to start feeling like there's no chance you'll survive.
* Very very flexible. It's a sandbox game. If you don't like something, toss it out. If you want more of something else, add it. In short, if you don't like the game, it's at least partially your own fault. This is the Mongolian Grill of board games. They've provided the ingredients, now you make what tastes good to you.
* Co-op. That's a plus for us. S3 adds PvP rules if that's your thing.
* Big but simple. The game has presence on the table, but despite dozens upon dozens of pieces in play, you'll rarely find yourself looking back at the rulebook once the game gets going (Exception: survivor skills. The names are "thematic" but not very descriptive. What does "Is that all you've got?" do? What about "Born Leader" or "Lifesaver"?)

Cons:
* Expensive. Way more expensive than it needs to be because there's more chrome than it needs to have. It's also annoying that you have to buy minis you don't want/need in order to get some of the more interesting spawn decks. Example: I already have quite a collection of Walkers (and S3 will add even more), but I'd love to have the spawn cards from the Walk of the Dead sets. $40+ for 24 cards is kind of excessive. Good News: There are three sets of the cards in multiple languages. The important parts of the cards are language independent so you may be able to find someone to split a set with you.
* The randomness of the equipment draw deck is the weakest part of the game for me. Sometimes you draw the best weapons in the deck on your first two or three searches. Sometimes you come up with nothing but AAAGH cards and crowbars while hordes of unstoppable (for now) fatties converge on you. Interestingly, it's the case where you pull too powerful of weapons too early that really ruins the game; being underpowered is more exciting than being overpowered. I'll reiterate that this is a sandbox game and you can certainly tweak things, I haven't yet some up with a "solution" to this "problem" yet. Incidentally, we ran a scenario where we both started with an ultrared weapon - one ranged and one melee - and could do no further searches. We compensated by adding more spawn points. Being able to kill zombies quickly means you're going to get to higher levels quickly which means the game gets tougher. And it did. Best scenario we've played yet.
* Lots of parts. Setup, cleanup and even play can take a long time if you're using the original game boxes. This is the only game where I went out of my way to repack everything in Plano boxes.

Neutral:
* A bit too "collectible" for my tastes. I don't care about the minis and the Big Bang Theory and other celebrity tie ins. Fortunately (for me) this is one of those rare cases when I was able to overpower my  completionism compulsions and convince myself that the special sculpts and survivor dashboards have no value to me and I could ignore them.
* There are a lot of rules wonks whining about the rule where ranges weapons will always hit survivors first. If you don't like the rule, don't use it! Give everyone the Low Profile skill or use one of the variants to add the ability to Duck. It doesn't matter. We like the rule and we play with it. It gives you an incentive to keep a melee weapon on hand (aside from opening doors). If you're on the fence about getting the game, do yourself a favor and ignore the ratings from people complaining about this rule. It's one of the easiest to house rule out (or maybe, like us, you'll decide you like it).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The rulebook is poorly organized and I seriously believe some house-rules will improve upon the game and make more sense, but Zombicide is a fun romp through zombie infested territory.
It doesn't take long to figure out the strategy against each type of zombie and a lot of it comes down to dice rolls, but Zombicide knows how to put the hurt on players when it needs to. The game never feels slow or boring. It's a very tense atmosphere.
What really shines is all of the different scenarios and how easy it is to create your own. The game is clearly open to some great expansion ideas too.
Overall: You get a lot for what you pay for. Tons of well crafted components and plenty of interesting stuff to keep you busy. Just don't let the rules hold you back.

RATING: 6.5
A game with amazing theme and components that just never seems to be as fun as I hope it will once it's on the table.  

The biggest issues for me:

(A) "Group-Think"  I love the idea of cooperative games, but a lot of them suffer from this.  I never feel like I'm playing a multi-player game as an autonomous survivor trying to co-exist with a group.  Instead, I feel like it always plays out as a single player game  where the group collectively decides what each hero must do at the start of the turn.  Ironically, probably one of those games that's BETTER for solitaire, if that's your kind of thing.

(B) Mission Balance.  The first mission was a nice "widow-maker" that was incredibly hard (perhaps too hard).  Some of the other missions, especially those with cars, just felt way toooooo easy and were a big let down after all the time and effort it takes to set-up and run through a mission.

While future expansions and new missions might address (B), I'm not sure what would have addressed (A) for me, and I ended up selling my Abomination copy [for a ridiculously huge chunk of change, so I can't complain].  Furthermore, since mission difficulty didn't scale with the number of players/survivors, the size of your group and how many survivors each player controls will go a long way to skewing a mission (e.g. 4 vs. 6 survivors).

RATING: 6
31-05-2014. Rated after 2+ plays. What I think about Zombicide I am not sure. I like many aspects of it, but dislike some others. I'll try to explain regardless.

As probably everyone will know you play a survivor in a zombie-apocalypse trying to survive and achieve some objective. I think I've played it 4-5 times in total and so far I have always lost and most goals were simplistic (get food, get these arms etc and get out..).

The components in this game are fantastic. Nice mini's, great quality boards although they look a little samey. The game itself is a very simple coop, in which each survivor basically take 3 actions and then a card is flipped to spawn monsters at each spawn point. Fun thing, the more experience with killing zombies you get, the more come out. Basically, you'll be overwhelmed relatively quickly by a large amount of zombies when you rush out and start killing.

I am not sure how I feel about the link between theme and mechanics. For example, when you shoot in an area with zombies, you always hit the survivor first. Why? Second, why are the missions lame and samey (get something, get out). Why do monsters get stronger if you get better in killing them? I understand why a game would want to do this, but it seems counter intuitive.

RATING: 7
Fast, fun, excellent ameritrash (from European designers). Dead on theme (pun intended), fast play, great coop, looks even more promising if you add expansions, gorgeous minis you simply itch to paint, not at all repetitive thanks to the scenarios. Notably better than any other zombie game I've played, compares well with them and shines. Handy to bring out as a filler, well worth spending a day campaign playing. Not at all a dice fest - yes, there are dice and you use them, but your tactics are way more important than the outcome of your rolls. I wish I'd been a crowdfunder and had gotten more content, but the awesome box with some of the best inlays I've ever seen is well worth the money spent. You get everything you need to play (with extras), and there's hardly a centimeter of wasted space inside. Extra care has been taken to pack the minis individually, which is awesome if you intend to paint them.

Edit: Had to upgrade my rating. This game sees a lot of play at home, and my SO loves it. When Season 3 is eventually released, and competitive teamplay is introduced, it may go even higher.

RATING: 10
This is one of the most fun and versatile cooperative games I've ever played. The endless combination of tile and equipment card configurations, open-ended objectives, character/enemy selection, and victory conditions make for infinite replayability.

You can run a complex campaign over multiple sessions involving changing maps with discrete objectives, or just lay out a simple map and see how many zombies you can take out. Depending on the scenario it can be a very difficult game; you won't win every time, and sometimes you need to sacrifice survivors to complete the mission, but I guarantee it's never the same game twice. My friends and I usually end up creating distinct personalities and back stories for our characters, especially for campaigns, turning it into somewhat of an RPG. And if you run out of scenarios, the Zombicide website has a great selection of PDFs available for free download.

It's a bit pricey up front, and with all the tokens and pieces you might want to also invest in a compartment storage box or even foam storage if you plan on painting your minis, but I feel like it's worth it. We've gotten so many hours of fun out of this game and I see no signs of slowing down.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Somewhat unpolished, but still fun. There is some strategy, depending on the scenario, and this is a compelling thematic game. The survivors play differently, and they must work together to complete the missions. Zombicide feels bit like a board game version of the zombie killing element of Zombieland. On the other hand, some of the missions are much harder than others, and at least one should have undergone more play testing. 

I like the way that the game incorporates random and push your luck elements, as the zombies behave in deterministic fashion, which allows detailed planning, but certain zombie spawn cards will give them extra activations or spawn zombies on sewer grates rather than their normal spawn points. You need to leave some room in your plans for those cards to come up, but as more and more zombies spawn, it can be difficult to do. Combined with the press your luck way that the attacks work in practice (should I keep attacking, or should I retreat. Should I give up on that survivor, or should I rush in and try to kill the rest of the zombies, thus risking both of us), there is a good amount of decision making. 

Some people have complained about the targeting priority rules. This rule works well in practice, as it creates tension between melee and ranged weapons. Without this rule, guns would always be better than melee weapons (except the Chainsaw). They could have made guns weaker by requiring ammo, but I enjoy the simpler rule set. It leads to enough decision making. This isn't a simulation game; don't expect it to be.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
I am hooked on Zombicide.

The miniatures this game is equipped with are fantastic in their detail; it can be intimidating to watch the horde develop, but so much fun to move them across the board. 

The different campaigns and double-sided gaming tile allow for higher replayability and interest, as you progress from a beginner to expert. The price may initially seem inaccessible until you play the game for the first time; this is a game you can play alone or with a group of people, play a different version of it each time, with different outcomes each time. This game is beyond the objective of just killing zombies and reaching the exit, which gives a fuller, more collaborative experience.

The website is an excellent resource for new campaigns created for the game, revised rules (the ones provided in my set were contradictory and have since been updated), and other information. 

I do hope for a character expansion set in the future; while you can create your own characters, I am such a fan of the miniatures provided that I would like them to be consistent.

Zombi hentelés ezerrel. A játék szabályai egyszerűek, karaktereinknek 5 helyes hátizsákja van, amiből kettő a két kezünk. 3 szintet tudunk a játékban lépni, amik különböző pluszokat adnak. 3 alap akciónkkal mozogni, támadni, ajtót nyitni, autót vezetni tudunk. Az egyes megszerezhető fegyverek piktogramjai könnyen érhetőek, a harc nagyon egyszerű, ahogy szinte minden a játékban. Talán a zombik mozgása a kör végén macerás kicsit. Ettől függetlenül kapunk egy egyszerű zombiölős játékot, ami a rengeteg szkenárió miatt bőven sok játékalkalmat ad. Egy kiegészítőt is próbáltunk hozzá és a 6-os pont mindenképpen eggyel több a kiegészítőket használva, ami még nagyobb változatosságot ad a játéknak.

Nem tudok igazán belekötni a játékba, mert az autóból kiszállás nélkül épületajtó nyitás is csak az egyszerűség miatt kerülhetett be a játékba. Talán a hentelés unalmassága volt kicsit zavaró. Illetve mégis van egy dolog, ami zavaró és nem jó, mégpedig, hogy a játék nehézsége nincs megoldva. Minél többen vagyunk annál könnyebb, ugyanis mindig ugyanannyi zombi jön bárhányan is játszanak. 5-en pont ideálisnak éreztem. Kevesebben valószínűleg muszáj egy embernek több karaktert vinnie. Nem volt zavaró a holtidő sem. Ez a játék más szemében akár jóval több pontos is lehetne, nálam most ennyi, illetve kiegészítőkkel 7-es. De teljesen jó játék.

RATING: 4
I am not sure about how to rate this game.

I personally try to rate the gameplay and abstract from the subjective or sentimental impression u usually get. that is the reason why i give a low rating.

Positiv features:
My friend, owning the game is a kickstarter backer (abomination or what it is called, when u bought the biggest pack). I was really impressed by the packaging, the top notch miniatures and the amount of stuff u get. There are so many well design miniatures it the whole bundle he got. Also the Artwork is really nice and gives the game a comic like splatter character. I like this.

On the other hand the map tiles look loveless. Example: Dividing the Areas by using pedestrian crossings is nice, but 1 crossing every 5 meters looks weird. A little bit more deviation like using cracks in the street, using cables or stakes/trees/barricades to mark the areas would have been better. (but still this would be a rating of about 8/9 for the artwork and game content)

Rulebook: This one is horror, but not in a good way. it really is nice in design but bad in reading or structure. moreover the scenarios are not in a well deweloped order (i cant remember if u get a storyline but i dont think so) (Still doesn lower the rating below 8)

Gameplay: This is really hard to explain. Many people like the gameplay and call it intuitive and it really is easy to learn and u get experience in controlling the zombies by your moves step by step. But the concept has alot of flaws that should not appear anymore for years.
Considering the Game a survival Horror/Zombie game with leveling Character i present the flaws i found and some changes i would like to see.
1.) It is survival but u have infinite Ammo for the weapons. I think this is contraproductive for decisionmaking and the flair of the game. it also contradicts realism (in a zombie apocalypse) and makes melee less important.
2.) Noise doesnt really have an effect on zombie spawns, zombie movement and attacks or deciding, which weapon u use. Survivors dont need to be quiet. killing is more important. Based on the rules every survivor counts 1 Noise even if he stand still. doesnt make sense. Zombies move to you even if thex dont see u and u dont shoot. Weapons that make no noise dont profit from this concept. 
Zombies should get extra spawn or movement when u are loud.
2.) Infinite searching in one room. I doesnt make sense that u can find 20 weapons in a toilet. ther should be like dice rolling for a search and a limit of stuff u can find. Also i would like to see, that the posibility to find stuff depends on the room you are in. Kitchen = Food, Bedroom/ weapons,..
3.) U cannot shoot zombies without shooting survivors first, if they are in the same area. stupid. should be more like: The chance to hit is like every roll of 1 is friendly fire (makes sense comparing shootguns or other blast weapons with rifles)
4.) ther is no way to react in the zombie activation. this is too static. you should get some choises to react with shots or escapeing/dodging.
5.) u cannot heal attacks. i think food p.e. could be used to heal, so survivors dont die and have to wathc others play for 2 hours.

Ofc the game lives by its house rules and custom maps and there is plenty of room to create excellent games and scenarios. But the points i present show, that the game testing wasnt sufficient. the official game rules and mechanics shouldnt have so many flaws when sold.

The game often becomes a mere search fest followed by a dice fest.people dont die due to bad decisions but pure bad luck, when zombies get multiple activation. u cant do anything then to save your arse.

I dont like pure coop games that much, but this one is abit dull. I put Gears of War way over this one, becaus eof the reaction possibility, cover and the action and damage system. also it has ammo loss as basic concept.

My ratings is based on high expactations that got diluted by poor game mechanics. Use house rules, i say.

RATING: 8
Components - .7/1 Box is solid, cardboard tokens for most statuses work just fine. Cards are small but usable, character sheets are so-so. Zombies and Player models are nice, but zombies are a pain in the ass to put away (slots in box aren't necessarily intuitive). Every time we say we're going to take a picture, yet never do :/

Fun - .8/1 Runs the risk of Alpha player. Generally a great experience, we try to focus play on keeping everyone alive in addition to completing the objective, which creates more tension.

Replayability - 1/1 Tiles are modular to leave a lot of flexibility. Enough components to create a multitude of scenarios if the original get boring. Ultimately enough randomness to be able to play scenarios multiple times.

Strategic - .8/1 Certainly a fair amount of strategy, between balancing kills between survivors, searching versus continuing on, thinning the heard versus claiming objectives, etc. Does suffer some from good strategies can be completely negated due to unlucky card draws (e.g. runners spawn right next to you, then get extra turn).

Theme - .7/1 Not a perfect zombie experience, but does capture the team against a never-ending horde approach.


Personal Rating - 4/5 I really like this game, and more importantly, my family (primary gaming group) really gets into this. My first real co-op game and it took me some time to dial back the Alpha gamer problem. Since getting that under control, people tend to enjoy themselves a lot.

RATING: 7
This is a very straightforward cooperative zombie killing game.  If this sounds like fun to you then you will probably enjoy it.

I liken this a lot to Super Dungeon Explore, it takes the dungeon crawl formula and streamlines it into where the players just mow down waves of zombies.  There are some tactics to consider but the rules system for collecting items, using weapons, spawning enemies, etc. are very simplified.  This makes it a very accessible game but it also doesn't make it the most deep or engaging game.  Still, this is certainly a flavor many people enjoy and it knows what it is and does it well.

Also, the game is gorgeous.  It comes in a giant box full of tons of miniatures, all of which are beautifully sculpted.  Plus one of the characters is drive-in diner girl wearing a skirt and skates and wielding a chainsaw.  How do you not just love that?

RATING: 6

RATING: 6.5
I'm never sure how to rate games that are clearly well-designed but simply do not suit my tastes. Zombicide is one of these -- a co-operative survival game where players scramble to find equipment while fending off ever-increasing hordes of zombies.

Production is superb, rules are simple enough to avoid a headache but complex enough to allow for thematic touches (e.g. noise) and real differentiation between characters.

If the time investment is too much for the level of luck involved, well, it's still an enormously playable example of "ameritrash" done right, with genuinely thematic mechanisms, great humour, opportunities for truly awesome or hilariously disastrous dice rolls, and, of course, buckets of plastic.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
I love this game. Makes an awesome compliment to Last Night On Earth as well. They are different in the most perfect ways that make them good to play back to back for even more variety.

The only things that keep this game from getting a 10 in my book are:

- The difficulty as you progress could use the slightest tweaking to be not quite as hard. Granted, I love that the S starts to hit the fan as you get further into the game, but it starts to get a little overboard and becomes darn near impossible to win. I think the difficulty could be tweaked to be just a teeny bit easier.

- It is also a little repetitive in that, for the most part, you are pretty much always doing the same thing. Other games I have played have different scenarios that can change very much so what you have to do. Granted, there is of course still the same basic gameplay behind it, but it still gives each scenario a different feel. Here, for the most part it is always just kill zombies and pick up the littel X's. There is nothing wrong with that, but a little variety could give it that extra kick.

RATING: 6
See my review!

 Brilliant co-op game. And it is a true co-op game. if you want to survive you'll need to agree a joint course of action and bring the group along with you. no lone wolfing it here. unlike other zombie games, you won't want to be charging into groups of enemies waving a chainsaw round your head. this is all about crowd control, keeping the numbers down, moving the zombies already on the board where you want them to go and keeping one step ahead of the extra turn cards. 

 I'm docking it a point for the rulebook. which is bad. and for scenario 02 which doesn't work, even the revised version.

**********

 edit: After a few more plays, i'm cooler on the game. it's still good fun with some great moments (Amy single handedly holding off the entire zombie horde with chainsaw until we were suddenly able to simply stroll to the exit), but it can be anticlimactic, with either every hero dying in 1 turn due to unlucky card drawing or the survivors simply strolling through, barely having to fire a shot in anger.
 The good thing is that we have the play time right down now and can now play 3 or 4 games in a single evening. It's still an eight, but i can see it slipping over the next few months. 

edit2: this hasn't hit the table in a good 6 months now. Still like it but I think it's become a once in a while game.

RATING: 6.25
Light weight zombie survival game, just a little too light weight for my tastes. The rules are really weird and there's ton of "logic gaps" and problems with it. The scenarios feel pretty samey -- run away and get some good items then run back and kill stuff. It is basically a glorified dice fest, and it isn't that bad, but it isn't good either. Balancing the kills and special abilities is the most interesting part of the game, but that isn't enough to stand on its own. Overall, if you're looking for a decent light co-op zombie game this one works, but don't get held up on the rules and feel free to change them to fit your play style.

RATING: 5
Visually nice zombie shoot-em-up game. Gives a good feel of exploration and powering up.
Game starts off fast paced, but really starts to drag as more zombies enter the game. Many of these will be on the other side of the board and have almost no effect on the game, except to reduce the zombie pool (running out of models is bad).
Plagued with numerous thematically stupid rules. Worse, much of the decisions in the game are about figuring out how to work around the thematic stupidity.
In a 2 player game, you use 6 characters each. A lot to keep track of, and it means you use ALL the characters in each game, which really reduces the feeling of variety.
Apparently major flaws in existing scenarios and extensive errata on the publisher's website.
Someone at CMON doesn't understand numbering. The tiles have random and incomprehensible numbering schemes, and scenario 10 is the best one for beginners while scenario 1 is the biggest, longest and hardest scenario.
+co-op+

Painted: 0/?

House rule: Just pick character turn order. Clockwise is a royal pain.

For a 6 Survivor Game or a 4 Survivor game on a 2x2 board
Divide the Zombie deck into two piles; the first pile with 16 cards and the second pile with the remainder of the deck.

Draw zombie cards from the small pile first. Zombie draws from this pile are at Blue threat level.

When this pile is exhausted, switch to using the second, larger, deck. Zombie draws from this pile are at the Yellow threat level.

When this pile is exhausted, reshuffle the entire zombie deck and use the full deck. This next pass through, the zombie draws are at the Orange threat level.

Should you exhaust the deck again, reshuffle. All remaining draws are at the Red threat level.

For a 4 Survivor game on a 3x3 board
Don't split the deck.
The first pass through the whole deck is at Blue.
Second pass at Yellow.
Third pass at Orange.
After that as Red.

This does not match the advancement nearly as closely, but with only 4 survivors on a big board you need the help.

Resilient Survivors for 4 Survivor Games
Survivors can take one extra wound. The first wound they take does not cause them to drop an item. To avoid running out of wound cards, simply place the first wound card on the character portrait on the card, then move it into a normal equipment slot when they take their second wound.

Other Stray Variants
No Zombie Amoebas: We simply roll for which direction odd zombies go, rather than having them split.

Tripping over themselves: Zombies moving via an extra activation card have a burst of speed, but tend to moving so hastily they trip stumble over each other in their haste to find tasty flesh. A survivor can never take more than one wound past toughness during a single extra activation card.
However, you can't simply pile up attacks on a character to waste them; the zombies will try to attack all the survivors in a space if possible.
Example 1: Ned and Wanda are in a space together and 5 zombies activate and attack them. They only take 1 wound each.

Example 2: A Tough survivor is attacked by 3 zombies. The survivor still takes 1 wound.

Example 3: A survivor with Tough and a survivor without it are attacked by 2 zombies. The survivor with Tough could ignore the first hit and take a wound on the second, leaving the other survivor unhurt. Or the other survivor could take the hit and the Tough survivor could ignore one hit, leaving the Tough survivor unhurt.

Note that this ONLY applies to bonus activations. If you just start the zombie turn with multiple zombies, you are devoured as normal!

The We didn't buy tons of extra zombie minis Variant: If there aren't enough zombies left to spawn new zombies, activate one zombie of the correct type for each model you are unable to spawn, rather than all the zombies of that type. You may choose which zombies are activated.

Aiming Carefully: You may spend 1 action to aim into a space with other survivors. Your very next shooting attack (including with dual weapons) ignores survivors. However, if you roll 2 or more misses on the attack (counting both weapons if you are using dual weapons), a random survivor takes 1 damage.

We don't actually bother with this variant, as the targeting rules don't really bother us, but it works out as a good simple rule to use.

RATING: 8
Check out my video review here: http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8TQjNTQ1Cvs
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
Whether this release was one of the greatest hoaxes ever perpetuated on the gaming universe,  or,   at long last,  the definitive zombie infested bliss -  is certainly one that is up for debate.  Undoubtedly,  you will know which soap box it is that I stand upon,  in very short order.

"There's a sucker born every minute" is a phrase that is often attributed to the late American showman,  P.T. Barnum - although,  in actuality,  it is a phrase believed to have been spoken by someone else,   in criticism of the gullibility of his customers.  In either case,  Zombicide sets out to prove that there is validity in that statement's content.

This game was drummed up more than John Bonham's Ludwig's.  

At a time in my life when my debtors would have been hard pressed to garnish my salary with even a sprig of parsley,  I was hypnotized into dropping a bundle on Zombicide,  despite the gnawing feeling that this was merely chrome in search of a game.

There is no x-ray vision required here.....this purveyor of revulsion is tantamount to a glass bottomed boat.  It won't be long before you see through the thin veneer of shellac that inefficiently canvasses the decadence beneath it. 

Fittingly,  one of the pledge options on Kickstarter sported the moniker "Abomination Level".

Henceforth.  I will pay heed to the abundance of telltale signs,  should they surround me again,  in a cacophony of premonitory lamentations.

RATING: 2
Wow too mechanical. The game mechanism is boring.  As your game character gets stronger with more skills/actions (by killing zombies) more zombies spawn. The better you get,  more and more zombies spawn. So why improve your character?  Random Zombie spawn generation without being synchronized to players increase in actions/skills would have been a better design. I will say the game has wonderful Production values -- A+ there. Would rather play CARNIVAL ZOMBIE
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Our gaming group was looking for a new co-op challenge, having seemingly exhausted "Arkham Horror." "Zombiecide" brought in a great challenge. The game also takes the zombie fun from "Zombies!!!" and leaves the malevolence behind - you actually get to have fun!

The tutorial is perfect, but a bit misleading - things get much harder after that. 

Playing with more than four players adds an interesting dynamic in that each player only has one survivor. This makes the NECESSARY sacrifice plays much harder to make. Also - like any proper apocalypse - things can go pear-shaped in a hurry, so sound strategy will take numerous plays to develop.

It's rare to have this much fun losing a game. It makes victory all the more glorious.

Special mention is necessary for the quality of the game: Miniatures are the best you will see in a board game less than $100. Map tiles are beautiful/grisly. Cards are great.

Thank you, CMON.

RATING: 3
This game's only success is the beautiful miniatures.  
The rulebook is, simply put, a disaster.  Instead of being more tense as more zombies come out, it gets more tedious.  Playtimes are out of whack; for the quoted "1 hour" you can have scenarios that take more then 4 hours or less then 35 minutes.  Character balance is nonexistent.  Weird victory conditions make it possible to play for hours, then draw a single rare 'extra activation' card and instantly lose the game when a single survivor dies.  Summed up?  It's just not fun.

See my long, controversial (but top-thumb'd) full review: http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/843543/total-lack-balance

RATING: 8
The true joy of Ameritrash gaming is in the narratives created while playing the game.  Zombicide excels at creating and telling those stories.  The rules need a serious re-write for clarity and I'm not the biggest fan of the way ranged combat works (though it isn't as bad as I had thought it would be before I actually played the game). Other than that rule and some unclear incongraphy, the game is just what I hoped it would be--a fun, dice-throwing romp. The number of missions, free mission design tools, and sandbox nature of the components, means the game should have a long life and remain the darling of house-rulers for years to come.

RATING: 7
Zombicide is a game that does not live up to its promise as far as the written rules go. The theme, artwork and quality of components really deserve some rule tweaking. On thing that really has to go is the make-an-additional-turn-with-one-of-the-zombie-types spawn card. This card makes any sort of planning or calculated risk-taking impossible and therefore discourages creative tactics. The first full scenario is hard enough without it! Another rule that has to go is the one regarding the placement of an extra zombie whenever a group of them cannot be split evenly between direction. However, with some house rules I feel like Zombicide is a fun, atmospheric and easy to explain boardgame. I am really considering purchasing it, even though its retail price is intimidating.

RATING: 3
[i]"Poor. Likely won't play this again although could be convinced."[/i]

This should perhaps be a 2 but it's so inoffensive and bland I'm not sure it qualifies.

Several mechanics just fundamentally don't make sense for the theme - most obviously zombies splitting in half or speeding up for no reason. The game has no sense of pacing at all, as though the creators had never actually watched a zombie film but created a game having merely heard about them. Objectives are boring "randomly search for cans" nonsense and players are actively encouraged to micromanage who kills what instead of being free to do the only remotely fun thing in the game - rolling dice to shoot zombies.

Even if all that were fixed this would be no more than an average dice rolling time waster.

RATING: 7
Review Date: May 2017

Positives: Simple to learn. Great Co-op Game for those who like minis and killing a lot of zombies! Beautiful production of models, some other components could (and did) improve with Black Plague edition (player boards). 


Negatives: Can lead to alpha gamer syndrome if not playing solo. Some rules make no real sense (shooting other players for one). Can become surprisingly mathy for such an ameritrash game. You either win with no challenge or get completely annihilated, very little middle room which is where the flavour is. Horrendously long setup and take down time


Conclusion: Needs some house rule fudging, but does exactly what it says on the tin
 

Score 7....easy kill, easy kill, easy kill, loot, repeat, repeat...get horribly crushed or win without threat

RATING: 6
The single biggest flaw in the original Zombies!!! is that it wasn't cooperative.  So Zombicide at least gets that part right.

Zombicide, overall, is at least OK.  I would play again, which is more than I can say for most of its zombie brethren: the countless Walking Dead games, All Things Zombie, etc.  There's light decision-making, endless searching, and more die-rolling than you can shake an apocalypse at.

Flaws do exist in the game, and if these were to show themselves repeatedly I'd be sure to quit the game forever.  I've gotten lucky so far, though, and the flaws have pretty much kept to themselves.  Just shy, I guess.

RATING: 6.5
Starts out slow but the action ramps up quickly. So far the scenarios have been pretty different from each other. Requires a lot of cooperation and timing since the spawn cards go by highest level among the group; you can't just have someone rip off a bunch of kills before everyone else is ready. The zombie mechanics work pretty well: walkers are an annoyance, fatties are scary, and runners are terrifying. Haven't dealt with an abomination yet. The minis are obviously excellent and the tiles look great too. I have a quibble with the building spawn rules but everything else seems fine. I wish there was more "junk" in the equipment draw deck. It's just a hair unrealistic that you'd find a machete, SMG, and katana all in someone's kitchen.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
[b]Initial comment while waiting for the game:[/b]
I'm incredibly excited about this game! It seems to be the zombie board game I've been looking for, something in the genre of the Dead Nation PS3 game. It's also seems close (in design goals) to the zombie game I've been designing on my own.

[b]Comments upon unpacking my two Abomination sets:[/b]
Holy cow! First, I have never seen a couple of games better packaged to not get banged up, scuffed or dented in transit. Kudos to Cool Mini or Not!

Second, I have never seen a game's components so well packaged to avoid anything breaking in transit from manufacturer to end consumer. This game eclipses even Days of Wonders and GameWorks titles in how well tightly everything was packed. I'm in awe!

Third, this game looks better than most other games I own. Great looking rule book with lots of well illustrated examples, and people must be a whole lot more sensitive to me, but I find the rules well written (barring a few translation snafus). The game comes with wonderful looking and greatly functional character sheets, high quality minis that should paint up very well, good dice, nice snappy cards, and thick cardboard boards and tokens.

[b]Comments after initial play:[/b]
The gameplay is very intuitive and reminiscent of a good coop shooter video game. This will likely become a huge favorite of mine.

Lastly, I love toolbox games such as this. I think it stems from my RPG background, but I love making my own scenarios, coming up with house rules, and other additions.

I highly recommend this game!

[b]Comments after being beaten down in scenario 01 twice:[/b]
This game's fun! I feel like I'm at the edge of my seat. I love how in the solitaire version you can choose the activation order of your characters, and wish this was featured in the multi-player game as well.

I love facing hordes of zombies. This game has become an instant favorite, and should get to the table frequently. My 13 year old daughter also enjoyed her first play.

[b]Comments After 8 Plays:[/b]
If I don't count Scenario 00, Tutorial, then I have won only one game in 7 tries. I've lost Scenario 01, City Blocks, 4 times, while I've lost twice and won once in Scenario 10, Small Town. I still cannot stop playing. After my first win, I thought I had found a working strategy, but pulling one of the 4 Extra Turn cards can really change all that in a hurry.

The complete randomness of those Extra Turn cards, and the Sewer cards to a lesser extent, is starting to bother me a bit. There are 4 Extra Turn cards, and 2 Sewer cards, in a deck of only 42 cards, and in all but Scenario 07, Grindhouse, and Scenario 09, Might Makes Right there are 4 Spawning Zones, meaning at least 4 cards are drawn per round in the game. You go through the deck in 10.5 rounds, if you don't break into any unopened Buildings. This means you will frequently see Extra Turns and Sewer cards that foil otherwise perfect plans.

Obviously the game needs this to an extent, I just feel like I have no control over it at all. Sure, I try to avoid standing in zones with sewers, I also to keep zombies at least two zones away, but that's not enough when it comes to the Runners.

Enough whining, and back to the game. :zombie:

[b]Comments After 16 Plays:[/b]
Once you get to know the tactics of the game, you can mitigate the luck of the draw some, you also must keep track of cards already discarded versus still in the Zombie deck.

I have upped my rating to 10, given that I have rarely had such an urge to just play the game around the clock. This game is pure fun to me. It is exactly the zombie toolbox that I wanted. Coming up with new characters, and scenarios is dirt simple, and very rewarding. I love Zombicide!

RATING: 3.8
So much potential here. Seriously, with a less punishing (although interesting) leveling mechanism and some form of barricading/defensive options, this would be a go-to game. As it stands, it's fun without being overly impressive. And it's somewhat annoying to witness potential like this fall short of greatness.

Edit 1/3/12:
Played about four or five more times and am putting the game away for good. Way too many problems. Lowering rating substantially. Good intentions, but poor, awful, terrible, blah execution. Shame.

RATING: 7.6
唯一的亮点就是模型和版图美工了，但本人作为一个十多年的生化危机fans，体验zombicide后，实在没有发现更多出彩的地方了，耐玩度主要体现在人物搭配及不同剧本的完成难度上。。。售价也不便宜，现在一个一个扩也接踵而至，价格嘛，你懂的。。。
【关键词】美式合作，丧尸群包围，扮演幸存者逃生，起手平底锅，升级技能，杀戮屠城，开车地图炮，全部近视眼，敌我通杀

【推荐度】中低
